{
  "content": "# Kubernetes apiserver Library: Subsystem Architecture and Extension Guide\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries](#1-subsystem-purpose-and-boundaries)\n2. [Key Components and Responsibility Split](#2-key-components-and-responsibility-split)\n3. [End-to-End Request Flow](#3-end-to-end-request-flow)\n4. [Server Composition and Delegation Chain](#4-server-composition-and-delegation-chain)\n5. [API Group Registration](#5-api-group-registration)\n6. [Storage Layer and Watch Cache](#6-storage-layer-and-watch-cache)\n7. [Extension Points and Customization Hooks](#7-extension-points-and-customization-hooks)\n8. [Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs](#8-failure-modes-limits-and-design-tradeoffs)\n9. [Operational Implications](#9-operational-implications)\n10. [Important Files and Directories](#10-important-files-and-directories)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\nThe `k8s.io/apiserver` library (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/`) is a reusable framework for building production-grade, Kubernetes-style API servers. It is the foundation for `kube-apiserver` itself and for extension API servers written by third parties (aggregated API servers, CRD-backed servers, etc.).\n\n**What it does:**\n- Provides the `GenericAPIServer` runtime: HTTP serving, TLS, lifecycle management, health endpoints.\n- Implements the full request pipeline: authentication \u2192 authorization \u2192 priority-and-fairness \u2192 audit \u2192 admission \u2192 REST dispatch \u2192 storage.\n- Offers pluggable backends for every stage of that pipeline via well-defined Go interfaces.\n- Bridges between the HTTP world and the typed Go world via serialization, conversion, and versioning machinery sourced from `k8s.io/apimachinery`.\n\n**What it does not do:**\n- Define concrete API types (those live in `k8s.io/api` and in individual API group packages).\n- Run controllers or reconciliation loops (that is `controller-manager` territory).\n- Talk to clients other than etcd (outbound calls to webhooks and extension servers go through `k8s.io/client-go`).\n\n**Upstream / downstream dependencies:**\n\n| Direction | Dependency | Role |\n|-----------|-----------|------|\n| Upstream | `k8s.io/apimachinery` | Scheme, runtime.Object, serialization codecs, GVK primitives |\n| Upstream | `k8s.io/client-go` | REST client, informer factory (used by admission webhooks and PAF) |\n| Upstream | `etcd` (via `go.etcd.io/etcd/client/v3`) | Primary and only supported backing store |\n| Downstream | `kube-apiserver` (`cmd/kube-apiserver`) | Main consumer; calls `CreateServerChain` |\n| Downstream | `k8s.io/kube-aggregator` | Aggregation layer; embeds `GenericAPIServer` |\n| Downstream | `k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver` | CRD server; embeds `GenericAPIServer` |\n| Downstream | Any aggregated API server | Extension servers built using `RecommendedOptions` |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 `pkg/server` \u2014 The Core Runtime\n\n**`Config` struct** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go:112`)\nThe central configuration object for `GenericAPIServer`. It is populated from command-line flags via `Options` structs and passed to `New()`. Fields include `Authentication`, `Authorization`, `AdmissionControl`, `FlowControl`, `AuditBackend`, `BuildHandlerChainFunc`, and `SecureServing`. Notably, it exposes `BuildHandlerChainFunc` as a first-class escape hatch for replacing the entire filter chain.\n\n**`GenericAPIServer` struct** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go:110`)\nThe server instance. It holds the `APIServerHandler` (which carries the live `http.Handler`), its delegation target, lifecycle signals, post-start hooks, pre-shutdown hooks, health registries, and the audit backend. The type does not export a `Start()` method directly; callers must first call `PrepareRun()` which returns the opaque `preparedGenericAPIServer`, and then call `RunWithContext()` on that.\n\n**`APIServerHandler` struct** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/handler.go:42`)\nHolds three layered handlers:\n- `FullHandlerChain` \u2014 the entire filter-decorated handler. `ServeHTTP` on this struct dispatches here.\n- `GoRestfulContainer` \u2014 the `go-restful` WebService container used for registered API groups.\n- `NonGoRestfulMux` \u2014 a `PathRecorderMux` for everything else (healthz, metrics, openapi, debug).\n- `Director` \u2014 chooses between the two above based on registered path prefixes.\n\n**`DelegationTarget` interface** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go:312`)\nThe delegation chain contract. Each server in the chain implements this; unhandled requests fall through to `NextDelegate()`. `emptyDelegate` terminates the chain, returning 404.\n\n**`lifecycleSignals`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/lifecycle_signals.go:112`)\nNamed channels signaling state transitions: `ShutdownInitiated`, `AfterShutdownDelayDuration`, `PreShutdownHooksStopped`, `NotAcceptingNewRequest`, `InFlightRequestsDrained`, `HTTPServerStoppedListening`, `HasBeenReady`, `MuxAndDiscoveryComplete`. Filters in the handler chain subscribe to these channels to drain requests gracefully during shutdown.\n\n### 2.2 `pkg/endpoints` \u2014 HTTP-to-REST Bridge\n\n**`APIInstaller`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/installer.go:62`)\nIntrospects a `rest.Storage` implementation at server startup and registers the appropriate go-restful routes for each supported verb (GET, LIST, WATCH, CREATE, UPDATE, PATCH, DELETE, and subresources). Routes are annotated with `x-kubernetes-action` and `x-kubernetes-group-version-kind` metadata used by OpenAPI generation.\n\n**Verb handlers** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/`)\nConcrete handlers for each HTTP method: `create.go`, `update.go`, `delete.go`, `get.go`, `patch.go`, `watch.go`. Each reads the request body, negotiates content type, calls into the admission chain, and dispatches to the underlying `rest.Storage`. For example, `createHandler` (`handlers/create.go:53`) deserializes the body only after the filter chain has authenticated and authorized the request.\n\n**`RequestScope`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/`)\nA per-route context snapshot containing the serializer, kind, namer, and admission interface \u2014 passed to every verb handler at dispatch time, eliminating repeated lookups.\n\n### 2.3 `pkg/admission` \u2014 Policy Enforcement\n\n**`Interface` / `MutationInterface` / `ValidationInterface`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/interfaces.go:122`)\nThe admission plugin contracts. `MutationInterface.Admit` may modify the object; `ValidationInterface.Validate` may only reject it. Both receive `Attributes` (operation, object, old object, user info) and `ObjectInterfaces` (convertor, defaulter).\n\n**`chainAdmissionHandler`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/chain.go:23`)\nA `[]Interface` that implements both mutation and validation by iterating plugins in order and short-circuiting on the first error.\n\n**`reinvoker`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/reinvocation.go`)\nWraps the mutation chain to re-run mutating plugins after any individual plugin sets `ShouldReinvoke()` on the `ReinvocationContext`. This supports webhook plugins whose mutations may invalidate earlier plugins' assumptions.\n\n**Built-in admission plugins** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/`)\nThe library ships with: `namespace/lifecycle`, `resourcequota`, `webhook/mutating`, `webhook/validating`, `policy/mutating` (MutatingAdmissionPolicy, alpha), `policy/validating` (ValidatingAdmissionPolicy, GA).\n\n### 2.4 `pkg/storage` \u2014 Storage Abstraction\n\n**`storage.Interface`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/interfaces.go`)\nThe storage contract defining `Create`, `Get`, `GuaranteedUpdate`, `Delete`, `Watch`, and `List`. The only production implementation today is `etcd3`.\n\n**`Cacher`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go:262`)\nAn in-memory write-through layer placed in front of the raw etcd client. It maintains a `watchCache` (a sliding-window event ring buffer) and a `cache.Reflector`. WATCH and LIST requests are primarily served from memory; only consistent reads must wait for (or fetch directly from) etcd.\n\n**`genericregistry.Store`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go:100`)\nThe standard CRUD implementation used by built-in and extension resources. It wraps `storage.Interface` in a `DryRunnableStorage` wrapper (to handle dry-run requests) and calls into resource-specific `Strategy` objects for validation, defaulting, and conflict detection.\n\n### 2.5 `pkg/util/flowcontrol` \u2014 Priority and Fairness\n\n**`apf_controller`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go`)\nA controller that watches `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevelConfiguration` objects and configures a set of `QueueSet` fair queues. When a request arrives, the controller matches it against `FlowSchema` rules (by user, group, verb, resource, namespace) and assigns it to a priority level.\n\n**`QueueSet` / fair queuing** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/`)\nImplements shuffle-sharding fair queuing. Each priority level has multiple queues. A request's queue is selected by hashing its flow distinguisher (typically `<username>/<namespace>`) against the queue count (shuffle sharding). Work is measured in seat-seconds via a `WorkEstimator`; list requests with many objects cost more \"seats\" than simple GETs.\n\n### 2.6 `pkg/audit` \u2014 Audit Logging\n\n**`Sink` / `Backend`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/types.go:22`)\n`Sink.ProcessEvents` receives audit events at each stage of a request. `Backend` extends `Sink` with `Run/Shutdown` lifecycle. Multiple backends may be unioned with `audit.Union`.\n\n**`PolicyRuleEvaluator`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/evaluator.go:40`)\nEvaluates the audit policy file against authorizer attributes and returns a `RequestAuditConfig` with a `Level` (None/Metadata/Request/RequestResponse) and stages to omit.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\nThe following describes what happens from the time an HTTP request arrives until a response is sent. File citations reference the actual construction order in `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go:1028`).\n\n> **Key insight**: `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` builds the chain from the _inside out_ \u2014 the innermost handler (closest to storage) is wrapped by successively outer filters. The code reads bottom-to-top in the source; the first handler to receive a request is the outermost one (last applied in the source).\n\n### 3.1 Filter Chain (outermost to innermost)\n\n```\nClient\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc\n[1] WithAuditInit               \u2014 allocates an AuditContext into the request context\n[2] WithPanicRecovery           \u2014 recovers from panics; logs stack trace; returns 500\n[3] WithMuxAndDiscoveryComplete \u2014 returns 503 if the server has not finished installing paths\n[4] WithRequestReceivedTimestamp\u2014 stamps arrival time into context\n[5] WithRequestInfo             \u2014 parses URL into RequestInfo (verb, resource, namespace, name)\n[6] WithRoutine (optional)      \u2014 offloads request to a separate goroutine (APIServingWithRoutine gate)\n[7] WithHTTPLogging             \u2014 structured HTTP access log\n[8] WithRetryAfter (optional)   \u2014 during shutdown, 429 + Retry-After header\n[9] WithHSTS                    \u2014 adds Strict-Transport-Security header\n[10] WithCacheControl           \u2014 sets Cache-Control: no-cache\n[11] WithProbabilisticGoaway    \u2014 randomly sends HTTP/2 GOAWAY to load-balance long-running connections\n[12] WithWatchTermination...    \u2014 drains watch requests during shutdown\n[13] WithWaitGroup              \u2014 adds non-long-running requests to a SafeWaitGroup for graceful drain\n[14] WithRequestDeadline        \u2014 enforces overall request deadline from context\n[15] WithTimeoutForNonLong...   \u2014 runs handler in a goroutine with a deadline; returns 504 on timeout\n[16] WithWarningRecorder        \u2014 installs a warning header writer (thread-safe under the timeout wrapper)\n[17] WithCORS                   \u2014 preflight and Access-Control-* headers\n[18] WithAuthentication         \u2014 calls Authenticator chain; injects UserInfo into context; 401 on failure\n[19] WithTracing (optional)     \u2014 creates OpenTelemetry span from authenticated context\n[20] WithAudit                  \u2014 emits audit events at RequestReceived and ResponseComplete stages\n[21] WithImpersonation          \u2014 applies impersonation headers (if Impersonate-* headers are present)\n[22] WithPriorityAndFairness /  \u2014 classifies request into a FlowSchema/PriorityLevel; queues or rejects\n    WithMaxInFlightLimit\n[23] WithAuthorization          \u2014 calls Authorizer chain; 403 on denial\n[24] (API handler / REST dispatch)\n      \u2502\n      \u25bc\n    Director \u2192 GoRestfulContainer \u2192 APIInstaller route\n                                        \u2502\n                                        \u25bc\n                                  Verb handler (e.g. createHandler)\n                                        \u2502\n                                        \u251c\u2500\u2500 Deserialize request body\n                                        \u251c\u2500\u2500 Default object fields\n                                        \u251c\u2500\u2500 Admission: Mutate (Admit)\n                                        \u251c\u2500\u2500 Validate (Strategy + admission Validate)\n                                        \u2514\u2500\u2500 genericregistry.Store.Create/Update/Delete\n                                                \u2502\n                                                \u25bc\n                                          DryRunnableStorage\n                                                \u2502\n                                                \u25bc\n                                          Cacher / etcd3\n```\n\n### 3.2 A Concrete CREATE Example\n\n1. **Request arrives**: `POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments`\n2. `WithRequestInfo` parses this as `{verb:create, resource:deployments, group:apps, version:v1, namespace:default}`.\n3. `WithAuthentication` validates the bearer token against the OIDC/x509 authenticator chain. UserInfo is injected.\n4. `WithPriorityAndFairness` matches the request to a `FlowSchema` (e.g. `system:authenticated`), places it in a queue for the `workload-high` priority level. The `WorkEstimator` assigns 1 seat (simple mutating write).\n5. `WithAuthorization` calls RBAC \u2014 checks if the user has `create` on `deployments` in `default` namespace.\n6. `WithAudit` emits a `RequestReceived` event.\n7. The go-restful `Director` identifies the path is registered under `/apis/apps/v1` and dispatches to the registered go-restful route.\n8. `createHandler` (`handlers/create.go:53`) is invoked:\n   - Content negotiation for request and response encodings.\n   - `limitedReadBodyWithRecordMetric` reads the body (up to `MaxRequestBodyBytes`).\n   - Decoder deserializes body into internal type (`apps/v1` \u2192 internal `apps`).\n   - Defaulting functions set optional fields.\n   - Admission `Admit` phase: mutating webhook plugins (and `MutatingAdmissionPolicy`) are called.\n   - Admission `Validate` phase: validating admission plugins (Strategy + `ValidatingAdmissionWebhook` + `ValidatingAdmissionPolicy`) are called.\n   - `genericregistry.Store.Create` is invoked \u2192 `DryRunnableStorage.Create` \u2192 `Cacher.Create` \u2192 `etcd3.Create`.\n   - `WithAudit` emits `ResponseComplete` with the response object (if audit level \u2265 `RequestResponse`).\n9. HTTP 201 Created is written back to the client.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Server Composition and Delegation Chain\n\n`kube-apiserver` is not a single server; it is a chain of three `GenericAPIServer` instances assembled in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go:CreateServerChain`.\n\n```\nIncoming request\n      \u2502\n      \u25bc\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Aggregator Server          \u2502  (kube-aggregator)\n\u2502  Handles: APIService CRD    \u2502\n\u2502  Proxies: extension servers \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n           \u2502 delegate (not an APIService path)\n           \u25bc\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Kube API Server (core)     \u2502\n\u2502  Handles: /api/v1, /apis/*  \u2502\n\u2502  built-in groups             \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n           \u2502 delegate (unknown path)\n           \u25bc\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  API Extensions Server      \u2502  (apiextensions-apiserver)\n\u2502  Handles: CRDs dynamically  \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n           \u2502 delegate (end of chain)\n           \u25bc\n      emptyDelegate \u2192 404\n```\n\n**How delegation works**: Each `GenericAPIServer` stores a `delegationTarget DelegationTarget`. When the `Director`'s `NonGoRestfulMux` cannot match a path, it calls the `UnprotectedHandler()` of the delegation target \u2014 effectively bypassing the *target's* filter chain (authentication, authorization, etc. run only once, in the outermost server). This is why `UnprotectedHandler()` returns the target's `Handler.Director` directly, not its `FullHandlerChain`.\n\n**Post-start and pre-shutdown hooks** are aggregated across the chain: each server's hooks are merged with its delegation target's hooks so that a single `RunWithContext` drives the entire system.\n\n---\n\n## 5. API Group Registration\n\n### 5.1 The `runtime.Scheme`\n\nThe `runtime.Scheme` is the type registry for a group. It provides:\n- **GVK \u2194 Go type mapping**: registers types so the serialization framework can create the right Go struct from a JSON/protobuf payload.\n- **Conversion functions**: the hub-and-spoke model converts all versions through a single internal type (the \"hub\"). `conversion-gen` generates most conversion functions; handwritten conversions handle non-trivial field renames.\n- **Defaulting functions**: `defaulter-gen` generates `SetDefaults_*` functions that are registered into the scheme and called during decode.\n- **Deep-copy functions**: `deepcopy-gen` generates `DeepCopyObject()` required by `runtime.Object`. This is safety-critical: objects returned from the watch cache must be deep-copied before modification to prevent data races.\n\n### 5.2 `APIGroupInfo` and Registration\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go:72\ntype APIGroupInfo struct {\n    PrioritizedVersions         []schema.GroupVersion\n    VersionedResourcesStorageMap map[string]map[string]rest.Storage\n    Scheme                      *runtime.Scheme\n    NegotiatedSerializer        runtime.NegotiatedSerializer\n    ParameterCodec              runtime.ParameterCodec\n}\n```\n\n`VersionedResourcesStorageMap` maps `version \u2192 resource-name \u2192 rest.Storage`. Each resource can have multiple sub-resources (e.g., `\"deployments/status\"`, `\"deployments/scale\"`), each with its own `rest.Storage` implementation.\n\n`GenericAPIServer.InstallAPIGroups` calls `APIInstaller.Install()` which:\n1. Iterates resources in `VersionedResourcesStorageMap`.\n2. For each resource, introspects which `rest.*` interfaces its `Storage` implements (`rest.Getter`, `rest.Lister`, `rest.Creater`, `rest.Updater`, `rest.GracefulDeleter`, `rest.Watcher`, etc.) via type assertion.\n3. Registers go-restful routes for only the verbs supported by that storage.\n4. Populates discovery documents and OpenAPI schema at the same time.\n\n### 5.3 The `Strategy` Pattern\n\nEach resource's `genericregistry.Store` is configured with up to three strategy objects:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go:172\nCreateStrategy rest.RESTCreateStrategy\nUpdateStrategy rest.RESTUpdateStrategy\nDeleteStrategy rest.RESTDeleteStrategy\n```\n\nA strategy object implements the resource-specific validation and business logic that is shared across all storage backends. For example, `Deployment`'s strategy validates pod template specs, resets fields that users may not set (like `status`), and enforces name generation rules. This separation keeps the generic storage machinery clean and resource-specific logic co-located with its type definition.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Storage Layer and Watch Cache\n\n### 6.1 Architecture\n\n```\nREST handler\n    \u2502\n    \u25bc\ngenericregistry.Store\n    \u2502  (wraps in DryRunnableStorage for dry-run)\n    \u25bc\nCacher  (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go:262)\n    \u2502   \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n    \u2502   \u2502  watchCache              \u2502  \u2190 ring buffer of recent events\n    \u2502   \u2502  cache.Reflector         \u2502  \u2190 LIST + WATCH from etcd\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n    \u2502  (falls through for consistent reads or cache misses)\n    \u25bc\netcd3.Store (grpc to etcd cluster)\n```\n\n### 6.2 Cacher Internals\n\nThe `Cacher` struct (`cacher.go:262`) maintains:\n- `watchCache`: a fixed-capacity ring buffer of `watchCacheEvent` objects, protected by an `RWMutex`. The buffer size defaults to 100 (`EtcdOptions.DefaultWatchCacheSize`), configurable per-resource via `--watch-cache-sizes`.\n- `reflector`: a `cache.Reflector` that issues a single LIST + ongoing WATCH against etcd for the resource prefix. Events are pushed into `incoming chan watchCacheEvent` and then dispatched by the cacher's main goroutine to registered `cacheWatcher` clients.\n- `watchers`: an `indexedWatchers` map that organizes active client watches by namespace and by an optional indexed trigger (e.g., for pod watches filtered by `spec.nodeName`). The trigger optimization avoids waking every watcher on every event.\n\n### 6.3 Serving Semantics\n\n| Request type | Served from |\n|---|---|\n| `?watch=true&resourceVersion=0` | In-memory ring buffer from the start |\n| `?watch=true&resourceVersion=<rv>` | In-memory buffer if rv is within window; otherwise etcd watch |\n| `LIST` (no RV, or `resourceVersion=0`) | Watch cache store snapshot |\n| Consistent `LIST` (`resourceVersionMatch=NotOlderThan` with progress notify) | Waits for cache to advance past etcd's latest rev; served from cache |\n| `LIST` with exact `resourceVersion` and a limit | Falls through to etcd (pagination not fully cached) |\n\nBookmarks (empty `WATCH` events carrying only a `resourceVersion`) prevent the cache's RV from becoming stale \u2014 a stale cache would force expensive relist operations on clients.\n\n### 6.4 Optimistic Concurrency\n\nEvery object stored in etcd carries a `resourceVersion` that maps 1-to-1 to etcd's global `mod_revision`. On `UPDATE` or `PATCH`, `GuaranteedUpdate` performs a `txn` in etcd that only commits if the key's `mod_revision` matches the expected value. A mismatch returns `409 Conflict`, requiring the client to re-read and resubmit. This is pure optimistic locking \u2014 no server-side distributed locks are held during request processing.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 7.1 Custom Handler Chain (`BuildHandlerChainFunc`)\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go:186\nBuildHandlerChainFunc func(apiHandler http.Handler, c *Config) (secure http.Handler)\n```\n\nBy replacing `Config.BuildHandlerChainFunc`, a consumer can insert, remove, or reorder any filter in the chain. The library ships two implementations:\n- `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` \u2014 the standard production chain.\n- `BuildHandlerChainWithStorageVersionPrecondition` \u2014 adds `WithStorageVersionPrecondition` (used by `kube-apiserver`) to gate requests until storage version migration is complete.\n\n**Risk**: Replacing the handler chain can silently disable authentication or authorization. Any custom chain should call `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` and wrap its result, rather than starting from scratch.\n\n### 7.2 Post-Start and Pre-Shutdown Hooks\n\n```go\n// GenericAPIServer method\nAddPostStartHook(name string, hook PostStartHookFunc) error\nAddPreShutdownHook(name string, hook preShutdownHookFunc) error\n```\n\nPost-start hooks run after the server starts listening, in separate goroutines. They receive a `StopCh` channel that closes when shutdown is initiated. Pre-shutdown hooks run before the HTTP server stops accepting connections \u2014 they are appropriate for draining outbound connections or flipping health check states.\n\n**Risk**: Slow or blocking post-start hooks delay the server's `HasBeenReady` signal, causing the process to be killed by liveness probes in managed environments.\n\n### 7.3 Admission Plugins\n\nAdmission plugins are the primary policy enforcement extension point. A custom in-process plugin must:\n\n1. Implement `admission.Interface` (and optionally `MutationInterface` or `ValidationInterface`).\n2. Register itself: `plugins.Register(PluginName, factory)` \u2014 where `plugins` is the `Plugins` registry passed into `AdmissionOptions`.\n3. If it needs shared resources (e.g., an informer factory or a Kubernetes client), implement the appropriate `WantsX` interface from `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/initializer/interfaces.go`:\n   - `WantsExternalKubeInformerFactory`\n   - `WantsAuthorizer`\n   - `WantsRESTMapper`\n   - `WantsFeatures`\n\nFor external validation without in-process code, `ValidatingAdmissionWebhook` (`plugin/webhook/validating`) and the CEL-based `ValidatingAdmissionPolicy` (`plugin/policy/validating`) ship with the library and require no code changes.\n\n**Risk of re-invocation**: Mutating webhooks may be re-invoked if a sibling webhook set `ShouldReinvoke()`. Plugins must therefore be idempotent \u2014 applying the same mutation twice must have the same effect as applying it once.\n\n### 7.4 Authenticator and Authorizer Composition\n\nAuthentication is composed via `authenticatorunion` (first-success wins). Authorizers are composed via a chain where each authorizer can return Allow, Deny, or NoOpinion; NoOpinion passes to the next. Adding a custom authenticator or authorizer requires modifying `Config.Authentication.Authenticator` or `Config.Authorization.Authorizer` before `New()` is called.\n\nFor extension servers, `DelegatingAuthenticationOptions` and `DelegatingAuthorizationOptions` (in `pkg/server/options/`) issue `SubjectAccessReview` requests to the main `kube-apiserver`, delegating all auth decisions \u2014 this is the standard pattern for aggregated API servers.\n\n### 7.5 `RecommendedOptions` for Extension Servers\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/recommended.go:34\ntype RecommendedOptions struct {\n    Etcd           *EtcdOptions\n    SecureServing  *SecureServingOptionsWithLoopback\n    Authentication *DelegatingAuthenticationOptions\n    Authorization  *DelegatingAuthorizationOptions\n    Audit          *AuditOptions\n    Features       *FeatureOptions\n    CoreAPI        *CoreAPIOptions\n    Admission      *AdmissionOptions\n    EgressSelector *EgressSelectorOptions\n    Traces         *TracingOptions\n}\n```\n\nThis struct is the standard entry point for building a new aggregated API server. Calling `ApplyTo(config)` applies each option group to the server config in dependency order (etcd \u2192 egress \u2192 TLS \u2192 auth \u2192 audit \u2192 admission). Extension server authors only need to set the fields that differ from defaults.\n\n### 7.6 `genericregistry.Store` Hooks\n\nThe `Store` exposes three sets of lifecycle hooks per operation:\n\n| Hook | Timing | Use case |\n|------|--------|----------|\n| `BeginCreate` / `BeginUpdate` | Before storage write; returns commit/revert | Acquire side-effect resources transactionally |\n| `AfterCreate` / `AfterUpdate` / `AfterDelete` | After storage write, before decoration | Emit metrics, invalidate caches |\n| `Decorator` | On every object returned from storage | Inject computed fields not stored in etcd |\n| `ShouldDeleteDuringUpdate` | During update | Implement finalizer-style soft-delete |\n\n**Risk**: `BeginCreate/BeginUpdate` revert functions must be idempotent because they may be called more than once if the framework retries internally.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 8.1 etcd Dependency\n\nThe `apiserver` library has a hard dependency on a live etcd cluster. There is no in-memory fallback for production use. A full etcd partition causes write operations to fail immediately (etcd requires a quorum write). Read operations that hit the watch cache can continue to succeed for cached data, but consistent reads (`resourceVersionMatch=NotOlderThan`) will block until `waitUntilFreshAndBlock` times out.\n\n### 8.2 Watch Cache Eviction\n\nThe watch cache ring buffer is bounded. When a slow client falls behind the write rate, its cached RV drops out of the buffer window and the watcher receives an `ERROR` event with `410 Gone`. The client must restart its watch from `resourceVersion=0`. This is a known operational cliff: high write rates or large ring buffer sizes (configured per-resource) directly trade memory for client resilience. The default buffer size is 100 events per resource type.\n\n### 8.3 Priority and Fairness vs. MaxInFlight\n\nThe library supports two concurrency-control mechanisms:\n- **`MaxInFlightLimit`** (`pkg/server/filters/maxinflight.go`): a simple counting semaphore with separate limits for mutating (`MaxMutatingRequestsInFlight`) and non-mutating (`MaxRequestsInFlight`) requests. Any request exceeding the limit gets an immediate `429 Too Many Requests`.\n- **Priority and Fairness (APF)**: replaces `MaxInFlightLimit` when `Config.FlowControl` is non-nil. APF queues requests rather than immediately rejecting them, and enforces per-flow fairness using shuffle-sharded fair queuing.\n\nAPF is the default in `kube-apiserver` since 1.29. Extension servers using `RecommendedOptions` do not enable APF by default and fall back to `MaxInFlightLimit`. APF requires `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevelConfiguration` objects in the API to exist before it can configure itself \u2014 creating a startup bootstrap dependency.\n\n### 8.4 Admission Re-invocation Overhead\n\nThe `reinvoker` wrapper (`pkg/admission/reinvocation.go`) can run the mutating admission chain twice per write request. With many heavy mutating webhooks, this doubles the worst-case webhook call latency. Operators should use `reinvocationPolicy: IfNeeded` selectively on `MutatingWebhookConfiguration` objects rather than globally.\n\n### 8.5 Handler Chain Construction Ordering\n\n`DefaultBuildHandlerChain` is built inside-out (code reads bottom-to-top). Misplacing a filter \u2014 e.g., moving `WithRequestInfo` after `WithAuthentication` \u2014 silently breaks features that depend on `RequestInfo` being in context (such as RBAC authorization, which inspects resource/verb). The framework does not validate the chain ordering at startup; bugs manifest at runtime under specific request patterns.\n\n### 8.6 Graceful Shutdown Sequencing\n\nThe shutdown flow (`RunWithContext`, `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go:536`) relies on a precise signal ordering:\n\n```\nSIGTERM/ctx.Done()\n    \u2192 ShutdownInitiated (readyz \u2192 red)\n    \u2192 PreShutdownHooks run concurrently\n    \u2192 AfterShutdownDelayDuration (~70s default)\n    \u2192 NotAcceptingNewRequest\n        \u2192 NonLongRunningRequestWaitGroup.Wait (up to ShutdownTimeout ~60s)\n        \u2192 WatchRequestWaitGroup.Wait\n    \u2192 InFlightRequestsDrained\n        \u2192 HTTP server stops listening\n        \u2192 AuditBackend.Shutdown()\n```\n\nA pre-shutdown hook that blocks longer than `ShutdownDelayDuration` can prevent the server from draining active requests cleanly. `WithWaitGroup` ensures that each non-long-running request adds itself to `NonLongRunningRequestWaitGroup` only if it is not exempt from `RetryAfter` logic, so these two mechanisms must agree on what \"long-running\" means.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Operational Implications\n\n### 9.1 Performance: Watch Cache Sizing\n\nEach watched resource type maintains its own ring buffer. Resources with high write throughput (e.g., `Events`, `Pods` in large clusters) should have their cache size tuned via `--watch-cache-sizes=pods#1000,events#0`. Setting a resource's cache to 0 disables caching for that type and pushes all watch traffic directly to etcd \u2014 useful for resources that are rarely watched but have large objects.\n\nThe metric `watch_cache_resource_version` (label: `resource`) tracks the cache's current RV. A value significantly behind etcd's compaction watermark indicates the cache is not keeping up and clients will experience frequent relist events.\n\n### 9.2 Performance: Admission Latency\n\nEvery mutating or creating request passes through the full admission chain synchronously. Slow webhooks directly increase P99 latency for all writes. The filter `WithAudit` annotates audit events with per-stage timestamps; the metric `apiserver_admission_webhook_request_total{name, operation, type, rejected}` and `apiserver_admission_webhook_latencies_seconds` track per-webhook performance.\n\nTo isolate the impact: a single slow webhook adds its full RTT to every matching request. Webhook timeout defaults are 10s; a webhook timing out results in a 500 (fail-open) or a rejection (fail-closed), depending on `failurePolicy`.\n\n### 9.3 Reliability: Health Endpoints\n\nThe server exposes three health gates via `NonGoRestfulMux`:\n- `/healthz` \u2014 liveness. Fails only on catastrophic internal state. Added checks via `AddHealthChecks`.\n- `/readyz` \u2014 readiness. Fails during startup and the shutdown delay period (as soon as `ShutdownInitiated` fires). Custom storage readiness checks can be added via `StorageReadinessHook`.\n- `/livez` \u2014 liveness with a grace period (`livezGracePeriod`) that allows the server to start up without being killed by kubelet.\n\n`MuxAndDiscoveryComplete` is a lifecycle signal used by the `WithMuxAndDiscoveryComplete` filter to return `503` for requests that arrive before all paths are registered. This prevents 404 responses from being cached by clients during server startup.\n\n### 9.4 Maintainability: Code Generation Dependencies\n\nThe `apiserver` library's build correctness depends on running several code generators before compilation:\n- `deepcopy-gen`: for `DeepCopyObject()` on all registered types.\n- `conversion-gen`: for conversion functions between internal and external API versions.\n- `defaulter-gen`: for `SetDefaults_*` functions.\n- `openapi-gen`: for `GetOpenAPIDefinitions()` used to build the `/openapi/v2` and `/openapi/v3` specs.\n\nForgetting to regenerate code after adding a new field is a common source of subtle bugs \u2014 the field will be silently dropped during conversion if no conversion function copies it, and will be missing from OpenAPI if not annotated.\n\n### 9.5 Scalability: Resource Version Monotonicity\n\nAll `resourceVersion` values are etcd `mod_revision` values \u2014 globally monotonically increasing across all resources. This simplifies consistency reasoning (there is a total ordering of all writes) but means the RV of a `ConfigMap` and a `Pod` are comparable in magnitude. Clients that filter watches by a very high RV may cause the cacher's `waitUntilFreshAndBlock` to wait indefinitely if the RV is ahead of the cache \u2014 exposing a denial-of-service surface. The `WatchCacheReadWait` histogram tracks time spent in this blocking path.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Important Files and Directories\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 ARCHITECTURE.md                          # High-level design overview (canonical)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 pkg/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 server/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 config.go                        # queue, request structs\n```\n",

{
  "content": "# Kubernetes apiserver Library: Subsystem Architecture and Extension Guide\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries](#1-subsystem-purpose-and-boundaries)\n2. [Key Components and Responsibility Split](#2-key-components-and-responsibility-split)\n3. [End-to-End Request Flow](#3-end-to-end-request-flow)\n4. [Server Composition and Delegation Chain](#4-server-composition-and-delegation-chain)\n5. [API Group Registration](#5-api-group-registration)\n6. [Storage Layer and Watch Cache](#6-storage-layer-and-watch-cache)\n7. [Extension Points and Customization Hooks](#7-extension-points-and-customization-hooks)\n8. [Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs](#8-failure-modes-limits-and-design-tradeoffs)\n9. [Operational Implications](#9-operational-implications)\n10. [Important Files and Directories](#10-important-files-and-directories)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\nThe `k8s.io/apiserver` library (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/`) is a reusable framework for building production-grade, Kubernetes-style API servers. It is the foundation for `kube-apiserver` itself and for extension API servers written by third parties (aggregated API servers, CRD-backed servers, etc.).\n\n**What it does:**\n- Provides the `GenericAPIServer` runtime: HTTP serving, TLS, lifecycle management, health endpoints.\n- Implements the full request pipeline: authentication \u2192 authorization \u2192 priority-and-fairness \u2192 audit \u2192 admission \u2192 REST dispatch \u2192 storage.\n- Offers pluggable backends for every stage of that pipeline via well-defined Go interfaces.\n- Bridges between the HTTP world and the typed Go world via serialization, conversion, and versioning machinery sourced from `k8s.io/apimachinery`.\n\n**What it does not do:**\n- Define concrete API types (those live in `k8s.io/api` and in individual API group packages).\n- Run controllers or reconciliation loops (that is `controller-manager` territory).\n- Talk to clients other than etcd (outbound calls to webhooks and extension servers go through `k8s.io/client-go`).\n\n**Upstream / downstream dependencies:**\n\n| Direction | Dependency | Role |\n|-----------|-----------|------|\n| Upstream | `k8s.io/apimachinery` | Scheme, runtime.Object, serialization codecs, GVK primitives |\n| Upstream | `k8s.io/client-go` | REST client, informer factory (used by admission webhooks and PAF) |\n| Upstream | `etcd` (via `go.etcd.io/etcd/client/v3`) | Primary and only supported backing store |\n| Downstream | `kube-apiserver` (`cmd/kube-apiserver`) | Main consumer; calls `CreateServerChain` |\n| Downstream | `k8s.io/kube-aggregator` | Aggregation layer; embeds `GenericAPIServer` |\n| Downstream | `k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver` | CRD server; embeds `GenericAPIServer` |\n| Downstream | Any aggregated API server | Extension servers built using `RecommendedOptions` |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 `pkg/server` \u2014 The Core Runtime\n\n**`Config` struct** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go:112`)\nThe central configuration object for `GenericAPIServer`. It is populated from command-line flags via `Options` structs and passed to `New()`. Fields include `Authentication`, `Authorization`, `AdmissionControl`, `FlowControl`, `AuditBackend`, `BuildHandlerChainFunc`, and `SecureServing`. Notably, it exposes `BuildHandlerChainFunc` as a first-class escape hatch for replacing the entire filter chain.\n\n**`GenericAPIServer` struct** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go:110`)\nThe server instance. It holds the `APIServerHandler` (which carries the live `http.Handler`), its delegation target, lifecycle signals, post-start hooks, pre-shutdown hooks, health registries, and the audit backend. The type does not export a `Start()` method directly; callers must first call `PrepareRun()` which returns the opaque `preparedGenericAPIServer`, and then call `RunWithContext()` on that.\n\n**`APIServerHandler` struct** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/handler.go:42`)\nHolds three layered handlers:\n- `FullHandlerChain` \u2014 the entire filter-decorated handler. `ServeHTTP` on this struct dispatches here.\n- `GoRestfulContainer` \u2014 the `go-restful` WebService container used for registered API groups.\n- `NonGoRestfulMux` \u2014 a `PathRecorderMux` for everything else (healthz, metrics, openapi, debug).\n- `Director` \u2014 chooses between the two above based on registered path prefixes.\n\n**`DelegationTarget` interface** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go:312`)\nThe delegation chain contract. Each server in the chain implements this; unhandled requests fall through to `NextDelegate()`. `emptyDelegate` terminates the chain, returning 404.\n\n**`lifecycleSignals`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/lifecycle_signals.go:112`)\nNamed channels signaling state transitions: `ShutdownInitiated`, `AfterShutdownDelayDuration`, `PreShutdownHooksStopped`, `NotAcceptingNewRequest`, `InFlightRequestsDrained`, `HTTPServerStoppedListening`, `HasBeenReady`, `MuxAndDiscoveryComplete`. Filters in the handler chain subscribe to these channels to drain requests gracefully during shutdown.\n\n### 2.2 `pkg/endpoints` \u2014 HTTP-to-REST Bridge\n\n**`APIInstaller`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/installer.go:62`)\nIntrospects a `rest.Storage` implementation at server startup and registers the appropriate go-restful routes for each supported verb (GET, LIST, WATCH, CREATE, UPDATE, PATCH, DELETE, and subresources). Routes are annotated with `x-kubernetes-action` and `x-kubernetes-group-version-kind` metadata used by OpenAPI generation.\n\n**Verb handlers** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/`)\nConcrete handlers for each HTTP method: `create.go`, `update.go`, `delete.go`, `get.go`, `patch.go`, `watch.go`. Each reads the request body, negotiates content type, calls into the admission chain, and dispatches to the underlying `rest.Storage`. For example, `createHandler` (`handlers/create.go:53`) deserializes the body only after the filter chain has authenticated and authorized the request.\n\n**`RequestScope`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/`)\nA per-route context snapshot containing the serializer, kind, namer, and admission interface \u2014 passed to every verb handler at dispatch time, eliminating repeated lookups.\n\n### 2.3 `pkg/admission` \u2014 Policy Enforcement\n\n**`Interface` / `MutationInterface` / `ValidationInterface`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/interfaces.go:122`)\nThe admission plugin contracts. `MutationInterface.Admit` may modify the object; `ValidationInterface.Validate` may only reject it. Both receive `Attributes` (operation, object, old object, user info) and `ObjectInterfaces` (convertor, defaulter).\n\n**`chainAdmissionHandler`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/chain.go:23`)\nA `[]Interface` that implements both mutation and validation by iterating plugins in order and short-circuiting on the first error.\n\n**`reinvoker`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/reinvocation.go`)\nWraps the mutation chain to re-run mutating plugins after any individual plugin sets `ShouldReinvoke()` on the `ReinvocationContext`. This supports webhook plugins whose mutations may invalidate earlier plugins' assumptions.\n\n**Built-in admission plugins** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/`)\nThe library ships with: `namespace/lifecycle`, `resourcequota`, `webhook/mutating`, `webhook/validating`, `policy/mutating` (MutatingAdmissionPolicy, alpha), `policy/validating` (ValidatingAdmissionPolicy, GA).\n\n### 2.4 `pkg/storage` \u2014 Storage Abstraction\n\n**`storage.Interface`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/interfaces.go`)\nThe storage contract defining `Create`, `Get`, `GuaranteedUpdate`, `Delete`, `Watch`, and `List`. The only production implementation today is `etcd3`.\n\n**`Cacher`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go:262`)\nAn in-memory write-through layer placed in front of the raw etcd client. It maintains a `watchCache` (a sliding-window event ring buffer) and a `cache.Reflector`. WATCH and LIST requests are primarily served from memory; only consistent reads must wait for (or fetch directly from) etcd.\n\n**`genericregistry.Store`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go:100`)\nThe standard CRUD implementation used by built-in and extension resources. It wraps `storage.Interface` in a `DryRunnableStorage` wrapper (to handle dry-run requests) and calls into resource-specific `Strategy` objects for validation, defaulting, and conflict detection.\n\n### 2.5 `pkg/util/flowcontrol` \u2014 Priority and Fairness\n\n**`apf_controller`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go`)\nA controller that watches `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevelConfiguration` objects and configures a set of `QueueSet` fair queues. When a request arrives, the controller matches it against `FlowSchema` rules (by user, group, verb, resource, namespace) and assigns it to a priority level.\n\n**`QueueSet` / fair queuing** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/`)\nImplements shuffle-sharding fair queuing. Each priority level has multiple queues. A request's queue is selected by hashing its flow distinguisher (typically `<username>/<namespace>`) against the queue count (shuffle sharding). Work is measured in seat-seconds via a `WorkEstimator`; list requests with many objects cost more \"seats\" than simple GETs.\n\n### 2.6 `pkg/audit` \u2014 Audit Logging\n\n**`Sink` / `Backend`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/types.go:22`)\n`Sink.ProcessEvents` receives audit events at each stage of a request. `Backend` extends `Sink` with `Run/Shutdown` lifecycle. Multiple backends may be unioned with `audit.Union`.\n\n**`PolicyRuleEvaluator`** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/evaluator.go:40`)\nEvaluates the audit policy file against authorizer attributes and returns a `RequestAuditConfig` with a `Level` (None/Metadata/Request/RequestResponse) and stages to omit.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\nThe following describes what happens from the time an HTTP request arrives until a response is sent. File citations reference the actual construction order in `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go:1028`).\n\n> **Key insight**: `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` builds the chain from the _inside out_ \u2014 the innermost handler (closest to storage) is wrapped by successively outer filters. The code reads bottom-to-top in the source; the first handler to receive a request is the outermost one (last applied in the source).\n\n### 3.1 Filter Chain (outermost to innermost)\n\n```\nClient\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc\n[1] WithAuditInit               \u2014 allocates an AuditContext into the request context\n[2] WithPanicRecovery           \u2014 recovers from panics; logs stack trace; returns 500\n[3] WithMuxAndDiscoveryComplete \u2014 returns 503 if the server has not finished installing paths\n[4] WithRequestReceivedTimestamp\u2014 stamps arrival time into context\n[5] WithRequestInfo             \u2014 parses URL into RequestInfo (verb, resource, namespace, name)\n[6] WithRoutine (optional)      \u2014 offloads request to a separate goroutine (APIServingWithRoutine gate)\n[7] WithHTTPLogging             \u2014 structured HTTP access log\n[8] WithRetryAfter (optional)   \u2014 during shutdown, 429 + Retry-After header\n[9] WithHSTS                    \u2014 adds Strict-Transport-Security header\n[10] WithCacheControl           \u2014 sets Cache-Control: no-cache\n[11] WithProbabilisticGoaway    \u2014 randomly sends HTTP/2 GOAWAY to load-balance long-running connections\n[12] WithWatchTermination...    \u2014 drains watch requests during shutdown\n[13] WithWaitGroup              \u2014 adds non-long-running requests to a SafeWaitGroup for graceful drain\n[14] WithRequestDeadline        \u2014 enforces overall request deadline from context\n[15] WithTimeoutForNonLong...   \u2014 runs handler in a goroutine with a deadline; returns 504 on timeout\n[16] WithWarningRecorder        \u2014 installs a warning header writer (thread-safe under the timeout wrapper)\n[17] WithCORS                   \u2014 preflight and Access-Control-* headers\n[18] WithAuthentication         \u2014 calls Authenticator chain; injects UserInfo into context; 401 on failure\n[19] WithTracing (optional)     \u2014 creates OpenTelemetry span from authenticated context\n[20] WithAudit                  \u2014 emits audit events at RequestReceived and ResponseComplete stages\n[21] WithImpersonation          \u2014 applies impersonation headers (if Impersonate-* headers are present)\n[22] WithPriorityAndFairness /  \u2014 classifies request into a FlowSchema/PriorityLevel; queues or rejects\n    WithMaxInFlightLimit\n[23] WithAuthorization          \u2014 calls Authorizer chain; 403 on denial\n[24] (API handler / REST dispatch)\n      \u2502\n      \u25bc\n    Director \u2192 GoRestfulContainer \u2192 APIInstaller route\n                                        \u2502\n                                        \u25bc\n                                  Verb handler (e.g. createHandler)\n                                        \u2502\n                                        \u251c\u2500\u2500 Deserialize request body\n                                        \u251c\u2500\u2500 Default object fields\n                                        \u251c\u2500\u2500 Admission: Mutate (Admit)\n                                        \u251c\u2500\u2500 Validate (Strategy + admission Validate)\n                                        \u2514\u2500\u2500 genericregistry.Store.Create/Update/Delete\n                                                \u2502\n                                                \u25bc\n                                          DryRunnableStorage\n                                                \u2502\n                                                \u25bc\n                                          Cacher / etcd3\n```\n\n### 3.2 A Concrete CREATE Example\n\n1. **Request arrives**: `POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments`\n2. `WithRequestInfo` parses this as `{verb:create, resource:deployments, group:apps, version:v1, namespace:default}`.\n3. `WithAuthentication` validates the bearer token against the OIDC/x509 authenticator chain. UserInfo is injected.\n4. `WithPriorityAndFairness` matches the request to a `FlowSchema` (e.g. `system:authenticated`), places it in a queue for the `workload-high` priority level. The `WorkEstimator` assigns 1 seat (simple mutating write).\n5. `WithAuthorization` calls RBAC \u2014 checks if the user has `create` on `deployments` in `default` namespace.\n6. `WithAudit` emits a `RequestReceived` event.\n7. The go-restful `Director` identifies the path is registered under `/apis/apps/v1` and dispatches to the registered go-restful route.\n8. `createHandler` (`handlers/create.go:53`) is invoked:\n   - Content negotiation for request and response encodings.\n   - `limitedReadBodyWithRecordMetric` reads the body (up to `MaxRequestBodyBytes`).\n   - Decoder deserializes body into internal type (`apps/v1` \u2192 internal `apps`).\n   - Defaulting functions set optional fields.\n   - Admission `Admit` phase: mutating webhook plugins (and `MutatingAdmissionPolicy`) are called.\n   - Admission `Validate` phase: validating admission plugins (Strategy + `ValidatingAdmissionWebhook` + `ValidatingAdmissionPolicy`) are called.\n   - `genericregistry.Store.Create` is invoked \u2192 `DryRunnableStorage.Create` \u2192 `Cacher.Create` \u2192 `etcd3.Create`.\n   - `WithAudit` emits `ResponseComplete` with the response object (if audit level \u2265 `RequestResponse`).\n9. HTTP 201 Created is written back to the client.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Server Composition and Delegation Chain\n\n`kube-apiserver` is not a single server; it is a chain of three `GenericAPIServer` instances assembled in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go:CreateServerChain`.\n\n```\nIncoming request\n      \u2502\n      \u25bc\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Aggregator Server          \u2502  (kube-aggregator)\n\u2502  Handles: APIService CRD    \u2502\n\u2502  Proxies: extension servers \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n           \u2502 delegate (not an APIService path)\n           \u25bc\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Kube API Server (core)     \u2502\n\u2502  Handles: /api/v1, /apis/*  \u2502\n\u2502  built-in groups             \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n           \u2502 delegate (unknown path)\n           \u25bc\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  API Extensions Server      \u2502  (apiextensions-apiserver)\n\u2502  Handles: CRDs dynamically  \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n           \u2502 delegate (end of chain)\n           \u25bc\n      emptyDelegate \u2192 404\n```\n\n**How delegation works**: Each `GenericAPIServer` stores a `delegationTarget DelegationTarget`. When the `Director`'s `NonGoRestfulMux` cannot match a path, it calls the `UnprotectedHandler()` of the delegation target \u2014 effectively bypassing the *target's* filter chain (authentication, authorization, etc. run only once, in the outermost server). This is why `UnprotectedHandler()` returns the target's `Handler.Director` directly, not its `FullHandlerChain`.\n\n**Post-start and pre-shutdown hooks** are aggregated across the chain: each server's hooks are merged with its delegation target's hooks so that a single `RunWithContext` drives the entire system.\n\n---\n\n## 5. API Group Registration\n\n### 5.1 The `runtime.Scheme`\n\nThe `runtime.Scheme` is the type registry for a group. It provides:\n- **GVK \u2194 Go type mapping**: registers types so the serialization framework can create the right Go struct from a JSON/protobuf payload.\n- **Conversion functions**: the hub-and-spoke model converts all versions through a single internal type (the \"hub\"). `conversion-gen` generates most conversion functions; handwritten conversions handle non-trivial field renames.\n- **Defaulting functions**: `defaulter-gen` generates `SetDefaults_*` functions that are registered into the scheme and called during decode.\n- **Deep-copy functions**: `deepcopy-gen` generates `DeepCopyObject()` required by `runtime.Object`. This is safety-critical: objects returned from the watch cache must be deep-copied before modification to prevent data races.\n\n### 5.2 `APIGroupInfo` and Registration\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go:72\ntype APIGroupInfo struct {\n    PrioritizedVersions         []schema.GroupVersion\n    VersionedResourcesStorageMap map[string]map[string]rest.Storage\n    Scheme                      *runtime.Scheme\n    NegotiatedSerializer        runtime.NegotiatedSerializer\n    ParameterCodec              runtime.ParameterCodec\n}\n```\n\n`VersionedResourcesStorageMap` maps `version \u2192 resource-name \u2192 rest.Storage`. Each resource can have multiple sub-resources (e.g., `\"deployments/status\"`, `\"deployments/scale\"`), each with its own `rest.Storage` implementation.\n\n`GenericAPIServer.InstallAPIGroups` calls `APIInstaller.Install()` which:\n1. Iterates resources in `VersionedResourcesStorageMap`.\n2. For each resource, introspects which `rest.*` interfaces its `Storage` implements (`rest.Getter`, `rest.Lister`, `rest.Creater`, `rest.Updater`, `rest.GracefulDeleter`, `rest.Watcher`, etc.) via type assertion.\n3. Registers go-restful routes for only the verbs supported by that storage.\n4. Populates discovery documents and OpenAPI schema at the same time.\n\n### 5.3 The `Strategy` Pattern\n\nEach resource's `genericregistry.Store` is configured with up to three strategy objects:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go:172\nCreateStrategy rest.RESTCreateStrategy\nUpdateStrategy rest.RESTUpdateStrategy\nDeleteStrategy rest.RESTDeleteStrategy\n```\n\nA strategy object implements the resource-specific validation and business logic that is shared across all storage backends. For example, `Deployment`'s strategy validates pod template specs, resets fields that users may not set (like `status`), and enforces name generation rules. This separation keeps the generic storage machinery clean and resource-specific logic co-located with its type definition.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Storage Layer and Watch Cache\n\n### 6.1 Architecture\n\n```\nREST handler\n    \u2502\n    \u25bc\ngenericregistry.Store\n    \u2502  (wraps in DryRunnableStorage for dry-run)\n    \u25bc\nCacher  (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go:262)\n    \u2502   \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n    \u2502   \u2502  watchCache              \u2502  \u2190 ring buffer of recent events\n    \u2502   \u2502  cache.Reflector         \u2502  \u2190 LIST + WATCH from etcd\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n    \u2502  (falls through for consistent reads or cache misses)\n    \u25bc\netcd3.Store (grpc to etcd cluster)\n```\n\n### 6.2 Cacher Internals\n\nThe `Cacher` struct (`cacher.go:262`) maintains:\n- `watchCache`: a fixed-capacity ring buffer of `watchCacheEvent` objects, protected by an `RWMutex`. The buffer size defaults to 100 (`EtcdOptions.DefaultWatchCacheSize`), configurable per-resource via `--watch-cache-sizes`.\n- `reflector`: a `cache.Reflector` that issues a single LIST + ongoing WATCH against etcd for the resource prefix. Events are pushed into `incoming chan watchCacheEvent` and then dispatched by the cacher's main goroutine to registered `cacheWatcher` clients.\n- `watchers`: an `indexedWatchers` map that organizes active client watches by namespace and by an optional indexed trigger (e.g., for pod watches filtered by `spec.nodeName`). The trigger optimization avoids waking every watcher on every event.\n\n### 6.3 Serving Semantics\n\n| Request type | Served from |\n|---|---|\n| `?watch=true&resourceVersion=0` | In-memory ring buffer from the start |\n| `?watch=true&resourceVersion=<rv>` | In-memory buffer if rv is within window; otherwise etcd watch |\n| `LIST` (no RV, or `resourceVersion=0`) | Watch cache store snapshot |\n| Consistent `LIST` (`resourceVersionMatch=NotOlderThan` with progress notify) | Waits for cache to advance past etcd's latest rev; served from cache |\n| `LIST` with exact `resourceVersion` and a limit | Falls through to etcd (pagination not fully cached) |\n\nBookmarks (empty `WATCH` events carrying only a `resourceVersion`) prevent the cache's RV from becoming stale \u2014 a stale cache would force expensive relist operations on clients.\n\n### 6.4 Optimistic Concurrency\n\nEvery object stored in etcd carries a `resourceVersion` that maps 1-to-1 to etcd's global `mod_revision`. On `UPDATE` or `PATCH`, `GuaranteedUpdate` performs a `txn` in etcd that only commits if the key's `mod_revision` matches the expected value. A mismatch returns `409 Conflict`, requiring the client to re-read and resubmit. This is pure optimistic locking \u2014 no server-side distributed locks are held during request processing.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 7.1 Custom Handler Chain (`BuildHandlerChainFunc`)\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go:186\nBuildHandlerChainFunc func(apiHandler http.Handler, c *Config) (secure http.Handler)\n```\n\nBy replacing `Config.BuildHandlerChainFunc`, a consumer can insert, remove, or reorder any filter in the chain. The library ships two implementations:\n- `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` \u2014 the standard production chain.\n- `BuildHandlerChainWithStorageVersionPrecondition` \u2014 adds `WithStorageVersionPrecondition` (used by `kube-apiserver`) to gate requests until storage version migration is complete.\n\n**Risk**: Replacing the handler chain can silently disable authentication or authorization. Any custom chain should call `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` and wrap its result, rather than starting from scratch.\n\n### 7.2 Post-Start and Pre-Shutdown Hooks\n\n```go\n// GenericAPIServer method\nAddPostStartHook(name string, hook PostStartHookFunc) error\nAddPreShutdownHook(name string, hook preShutdownHookFunc) error\n```\n\nPost-start hooks run after the server starts listening, in separate goroutines. They receive a `StopCh` channel that closes when shutdown is initiated. Pre-shutdown hooks run before the HTTP server stops accepting connections \u2014 they are appropriate for draining outbound connections or flipping health check states.\n\n**Risk**: Slow or blocking post-start hooks delay the server's `HasBeenReady` signal, causing the process to be killed by liveness probes in managed environments.\n\n### 7.3 Admission Plugins\n\nAdmission plugins are the primary policy enforcement extension point. A custom in-process plugin must:\n\n1. Implement `admission.Interface` (and optionally `MutationInterface` or `ValidationInterface`).\n2. Register itself: `plugins.Register(PluginName, factory)` \u2014 where `plugins` is the `Plugins` registry passed into `AdmissionOptions`.\n3. If it needs shared resources (e.g., an informer factory or a Kubernetes client), implement the appropriate `WantsX` interface from `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/initializer/interfaces.go`:\n   - `WantsExternalKubeInformerFactory`\n   - `WantsAuthorizer`\n   - `WantsRESTMapper`\n   - `WantsFeatures`\n\nFor external validation without in-process code, `ValidatingAdmissionWebhook` (`plugin/webhook/validating`) and the CEL-based `ValidatingAdmissionPolicy` (`plugin/policy/validating`) ship with the library and require no code changes.\n\n**Risk of re-invocation**: Mutating webhooks may be re-invoked if a sibling webhook set `ShouldReinvoke()`. Plugins must therefore be idempotent \u2014 applying the same mutation twice must have the same effect as applying it once.\n\n### 7.4 Authenticator and Authorizer Composition\n\nAuthentication is composed via `authenticatorunion` (first-success wins). Authorizers are composed via a chain where each authorizer can return Allow, Deny, or NoOpinion; NoOpinion passes to the next. Adding a custom authenticator or authorizer requires modifying `Config.Authentication.Authenticator` or `Config.Authorization.Authorizer` before `New()` is called.\n\nFor extension servers, `DelegatingAuthenticationOptions` and `DelegatingAuthorizationOptions` (in `pkg/server/options/`) issue `SubjectAccessReview` requests to the main `kube-apiserver`, delegating all auth decisions \u2014 this is the standard pattern for aggregated API servers.\n\n### 7.5 `RecommendedOptions` for Extension Servers\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/recommended.go:34\ntype RecommendedOptions struct {\n    Etcd           *EtcdOptions\n    SecureServing  *SecureServingOptionsWithLoopback\n    Authentication *DelegatingAuthenticationOptions\n    Authorization  *DelegatingAuthorizationOptions\n    Audit          *AuditOptions\n    Features       *FeatureOptions\n    CoreAPI        *CoreAPIOptions\n    Admission      *AdmissionOptions\n    EgressSelector *EgressSelectorOptions\n    Traces         *TracingOptions\n}\n```\n\nThis struct is the standard entry point for building a new aggregated API server. Calling `ApplyTo(config)` applies each option group to the server config in dependency order (etcd \u2192 egress \u2192 TLS \u2192 auth \u2192 audit \u2192 admission). Extension server authors only need to set the fields that differ from defaults.\n\n### 7.6 `genericregistry.Store` Hooks\n\nThe `Store` exposes three sets of lifecycle hooks per operation:\n\n| Hook | Timing | Use case |\n|------|--------|----------|\n| `BeginCreate` / `BeginUpdate` | Before storage write; returns commit/revert | Acquire side-effect resources transactionally |\n| `AfterCreate` / `AfterUpdate` / `AfterDelete` | After storage write, before decoration | Emit metrics, invalidate caches |\n| `Decorator` | On every object returned from storage | Inject computed fields not stored in etcd |\n| `ShouldDeleteDuringUpdate` | During update | Implement finalizer-style soft-delete |\n\n**Risk**: `BeginCreate/BeginUpdate` revert functions must be idempotent because they may be called more than once if the framework retries internally.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 8.1 etcd Dependency\n\nThe `apiserver` library has a hard dependency on a live etcd cluster. There is no in-memory fallback for production use. A full etcd partition causes write operations to fail immediately (etcd requires a quorum write). Read operations that hit the watch cache can continue to succeed for cached data, but consistent reads (`resourceVersionMatch=NotOlderThan`) will block until `waitUntilFreshAndBlock` times out.\n\n### 8.2 Watch Cache Eviction\n\nThe watch cache ring buffer is bounded. When a slow client falls behind the write rate, its cached RV drops out of the buffer window and the watcher receives an `ERROR` event with `410 Gone`. The client must restart its watch from `resourceVersion=0`. This is a known operational cliff: high write rates or large ring buffer sizes (configured per-resource) directly trade memory for client resilience. The default buffer size is 100 events per resource type.\n\n### 8.3 Priority and Fairness vs. MaxInFlight\n\nThe library supports two concurrency-control mechanisms:\n- **`MaxInFlightLimit`** (`pkg/server/filters/maxinflight.go`): a simple counting semaphore with separate limits for mutating (`MaxMutatingRequestsInFlight`) and non-mutating (`MaxRequestsInFlight`) requests. Any request exceeding the limit gets an immediate `429 Too Many Requests`.\n- **Priority and Fairness (APF)**: replaces `MaxInFlightLimit` when `Config.FlowControl` is non-nil. APF queues requests rather than immediately rejecting them, and enforces per-flow fairness using shuffle-sharded fair queuing.\n\nAPF is the default in `kube-apiserver` since 1.29. Extension servers using `RecommendedOptions` do not enable APF by default and fall back to `MaxInFlightLimit`. APF requires `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevelConfiguration` objects in the API to exist before it can configure itself \u2014 creating a startup bootstrap dependency.\n\n### 8.4 Admission Re-invocation Overhead\n\nThe `reinvoker` wrapper (`pkg/admission/reinvocation.go`) can run the mutating admission chain twice per write request. With many heavy mutating webhooks, this doubles the worst-case webhook call latency. Operators should use `reinvocationPolicy: IfNeeded` selectively on `MutatingWebhookConfiguration` objects rather than globally.\n\n### 8.5 Handler Chain Construction Ordering\n\n`DefaultBuildHandlerChain` is built inside-out (code reads bottom-to-top). Misplacing a filter \u2014 e.g., moving `WithRequestInfo` after `WithAuthentication` \u2014 silently breaks features that depend on `RequestInfo` being in context (such as RBAC authorization, which inspects resource/verb). The framework does not validate the chain ordering at startup; bugs manifest at runtime under specific request patterns.\n\n### 8.6 Graceful Shutdown Sequencing\n\nThe shutdown flow (`RunWithContext`, `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go:536`) relies on a precise signal ordering:\n\n```\nSIGTERM/ctx.Done()\n    \u2192 ShutdownInitiated (readyz \u2192 red)\n    \u2192 PreShutdownHooks run concurrently\n    \u2192 AfterShutdownDelayDuration (~70s default)\n    \u2192 NotAcceptingNewRequest\n        \u2192 NonLongRunningRequestWaitGroup.Wait (up to ShutdownTimeout ~60s)\n        \u2192 WatchRequestWaitGroup.Wait\n    \u2192 InFlightRequestsDrained\n        \u2192 HTTP server stops listening\n        \u2192 AuditBackend.Shutdown()\n```\n\nA pre-shutdown hook that blocks longer than `ShutdownDelayDuration` can prevent the server from draining active requests cleanly. `WithWaitGroup` ensures that each non-long-running request adds itself to `NonLongRunningRequestWaitGroup` only if it is not exempt from `RetryAfter` logic, so these two mechanisms must agree on what \"long-running\" means.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Operational Implications\n\n### 9.1 Performance: Watch Cache Sizing\n\nEach watched resource type maintains its own ring buffer. Resources with high write throughput (e.g., `Events`, `Pods` in large clusters) should have their cache size tuned via `--watch-cache-sizes=pods#1000,events#0`. Setting a resource's cache to 0 disables caching for that type and pushes all watch traffic directly to etcd \u2014 useful for resources that are rarely watched but have large objects.\n\nThe metric `watch_cache_resource_version` (label: `resource`) tracks the cache's current RV. A value significantly behind etcd's compaction watermark indicates the cache is not keeping up and clients will experience frequent relist events.\n\n### 9.2 Performance: Admission Latency\n\nEvery mutating or creating request passes through the full admission chain synchronously. Slow webhooks directly increase P99 latency for all writes. The filter `WithAudit` annotates audit events with per-stage timestamps; the metric `apiserver_admission_webhook_request_total{name, operation, type, rejected}` and `apiserver_admission_webhook_latencies_seconds` track per-webhook performance.\n\nTo isolate the impact: a single slow webhook adds its full RTT to every matching request. Webhook timeout defaults are 10s; a webhook timing out results in a 500 (fail-open) or a rejection (fail-closed), depending on `failurePolicy`.\n\n### 9.3 Reliability: Health Endpoints\n\nThe server exposes three health gates via `NonGoRestfulMux`:\n- `/healthz` \u2014 liveness. Fails only on catastrophic internal state. Added checks via `AddHealthChecks`.\n- `/readyz` \u2014 readiness. Fails during startup and the shutdown delay period (as soon as `ShutdownInitiated` fires). Custom storage readiness checks can be added via `StorageReadinessHook`.\n- `/livez` \u2014 liveness with a grace period (`livezGracePeriod`) that allows the server to start up without being killed by kubelet.\n\n`MuxAndDiscoveryComplete` is a lifecycle signal used by the `WithMuxAndDiscoveryComplete` filter to return `503` for requests that arrive before all paths are registered. This prevents 404 responses from being cached by clients during server startup.\n\n### 9.4 Maintainability: Code Generation Dependencies\n\nThe `apiserver` library's build correctness depends on running several code generators before compilation:\n- `deepcopy-gen`: for `DeepCopyObject()` on all registered types.\n- `conversion-gen`: for conversion functions between internal and external API versions.\n- `defaulter-gen`: for `SetDefaults_*` functions.\n- `openapi-gen`: for `GetOpenAPIDefinitions()` used to build the `/openapi/v2` and `/openapi/v3` specs.\n\nForgetting to regenerate code after adding a new field is a common source of subtle bugs \u2014 the field will be silently dropped during conversion if no conversion function copies it, and will be missing from OpenAPI if not annotated.\n\n### 9.5 Scalability: Resource Version Monotonicity\n\nAll `resourceVersion` values are etcd `mod_revision` values \u2014 globally monotonically increasing across all resources. This simplifies consistency reasoning (there is a total ordering of all writes) but means the RV of a `ConfigMap` and a `Pod` are comparable in magnitude. Clients that filter watches by a very high RV may cause the cacher's `waitUntilFreshAndBlock` to wait indefinitely if the RV is ahead of the cache \u2014 exposing a denial-of-service surface. The `WatchCacheReadWait` histogram tracks time spent in this blocking path.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Important Files and Directories\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 ARCHITECTURE.md                          # High-level design overview (canonical)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 pkg/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 server/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 config.go                        # ## Table of Contents

## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries

The `k8s.io/apiserver` library (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/`) is a reusable framework for building production-grade, Kubernetes-style API servers. It is the foundation for `kube-apiserver` itself and for extension API servers written by third parties (aggregated API servers, CRD-backed servers, etc.).

**What it does:**
- Provides the `GenericAPIServer` runtime: HTTP serving, TLS, lifecycle management, health endpoints.
- Implements the full request pipeline: authentication → authorization → priority-and-fairness → audit → admission → REST dispatch → storage.
- Offers pluggable backends for every stage of that pipeline via well-defined Go interfaces.
- Bridges between the HTTP world and the typed Go world via serialization, conversion, and versioning machinery sourced from `k8s.io/apimachinery`.

**What it does not do:**
- Define concrete API types (those live in `k8s.io/api` and in ind
